Looked on their website for the brush cleaner and it says powder products can be washed off with soap and water but cream products you need to use their own cleaning powder. Love you Bunny!!!
SO, here's my suggestions. Do an initial wash of 10 seconds , spin, 10 seconds with the 1st soapy water on all the brushes, Then change the water and  use only clean water and do another wash and spin with clean water ( no soap ). If you want to you can also use alcohol in the basin for your cream base brushes and then after words, do a wash spin cycle with soap and water.  You can also use really inexpensive baby shampoo to do your brushes (unless you have other issues with sensitive skin)

Also, I think there are a lot of great things to this product, but it feels more like a prewash than an actual good ol' fashion washing of brushes. For one thing, even when you dry it, there is still probably soap residue left on the brush since it wasn't rinsed in clean water before drying. Another thing that freaks me out is how much it spreads out the bristles, and the force of the spinning making the bristles much looser on the brush. Unless you had a brush guard or something to put the bristles back together in its original shape, I can't see this being good for the functionality of the brush. (;_; )

Ohh, Bunny,the word 'apropos' doesn't NOT mean 'appropriate' and shouldn't be used as its substitute. It means more like 'by the way' or 'along those lines...'. As in, 'Apropos of makeup washing tools, have you ever tried Brand x brush soap?' The emphasis on the last syllable, 'proh', and the last 's' is silent.

Just FYI....soap molecules work by attracting dirt. So as you use your brush on your face (because it still has soap on it) you'll be putting soap on your skin which will attract dirt all day. So it might be a good idea to repeat the washing procedure again,  without soap in the water. At least,  that's what i would do:)

Think you should try lukewarm or a little warmer water for the creamy make-up. Hey Bunny Something I learned when our inspector came in ( Im a hair stylist) was that anything over 70% alcohol really does nothing as it's so high that it evaporates to fast. He said to use 70-71% only as it stays long enough to kill any potential bacteria.

This product seems pretty neat, but I think it would be much better if it mentioned a rinsing step. What I do is do a once over wash on all of them with the same liquid and then I change the liquid and do them all again. if I notice the water is getting cloudier than just from soap/it foaming from the spinning I'll change it again. But it's so worth it if you're prone to acne or just clogged pores, irritation etc. I have rosacea and occasional cystic acne outbreaks along with generally just sensitive skin so it's wonderful imo.  I do witch hazel or tea tree instead of alcohol btw, it's still antiseptic but it's way less drying on the brushes.
